## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the population growth rate (dP/dt) as a function of time and current population size, which is a classic population dynamics problem. The relationship likely involves density-dependent growth models where the growth rate depends on the current population level.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Malthusian (exponential) growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P', 'scenario': 'Unlimited exponential growth, rate proportional to population'}
- {'name': 'Logistic growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P)', 'scenario': 'Density-dependent growth with carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Theta-logistic growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)', 'scenario': 'Generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence'}
- {'name': 'Gompertz growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P)', 'scenario': 'Growth rate decreasing logarithmically with population'}
- {'name': 'Allee effect growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P)', 'scenario': 'Growth with minimum viable population threshold (strong Allee effect)'}
- {'name': 'Von Bertalanffy-type growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Growth as balance between anabolic and catabolic processes'}
- {'name': 'Richards growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) / c2', 'scenario': 'Flexible asymmetric sigmoidal growth'}
- {'name': 'Power-law growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1', 'scenario': 'Scaling relationship between growth rate and population'}
- {'name': 'Quadratic density dependence', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2', 'scenario': 'Growth with linear and quadratic density terms'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent Malthusian rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'Exponential growth with time-varying intrinsic rate'}
- {'name': 'Beverton-Holt continuous form', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Growth with density-dependent recruitment and constant mortality'}
- {'name': 'Polynomial density dependence with cubic term', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3', 'scenario': 'Higher-order density-dependent effects including Allee-like behavior'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent negative feedback → multiplicative factor (1 - c*P) or (1 - (c*P)**n) limiting growth at high population
- Allee effect (positive density dependence at low P) → additional multiplicative factor (P - c) introducing a lower critical threshold
- Logarithmic saturation in growth → log(c/P) term as in Gompertz model, giving slower deceleration than logistic
- Metabolic scaling → fractional power P**c1 with c1 between 0 and 1, reflecting allometric scaling of biological rates
- Competing gain and loss processes → difference of two power-law terms c0*P**a - c1*P**b representing anabolism vs catabolism
- Time-modulated growth → multiplicative time-dependent factor such as sin(c*t) or exp(c*t) representing seasonal or environmental change
- Inflection point asymmetry → generalized exponent in (1 - (c*P)**c2) controlling where maximum growth rate occurs relative to carrying capacity
- Ratio-dependent effects → terms like P/(P + c) indicating saturating functional responses in self-limitation

## GT Analysis

The GT is:
```
0.13870625668024555*(-1 + P/8.038138014396704)*(1 - P/70.01799944958296)*P + 0.13870625668024555*(1 - P/70.01799944958296)*P + 0.13870625668024555*P/(1 + exp(-8.038138014396704*(-0.5894251550796137 + P)))
```

Let me simplify. Let me denote α = 0.13870625668024555, a = 8.038138014396704, b = 70.01799944958296, d = 0.5894251550796137.

GT = α*(-1 + P/a)*(1 - P/b)*P + α*(1 - P/b)*P + α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(-d + P)))

First two terms: factor out α*(1 - P/b)*P:
= α*(1 - P/b)*P * [(-1 + P/a) + 1] + α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(P - d)))
= α*(1 - P/b)*P * (P/a) + α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(P - d)))
= α*P²/(a*b) * (b - P)/1... wait, let me redo:

= α*(P/a)*(1 - P/b)*P + α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(P-d)))
= (α/a)*P²*(1 - P/b) + α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(P-d)))
= (α/a)*P² - (α/(a*b))*P³ + α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(P-d)))

So GT = -(α/(ab))*P³ + (α/a)*P² + α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(P-d)))

This is a cubic polynomial in P plus a sigmoid-like term: **P³ term + P² term + sigmoid term involving P/(1+exp(...))**.

The sigmoid term α*P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))) can be rewritten. Note that 1/(1+exp(-x)) is the logistic/sigmoid function, and for large positive x it approaches 1, for large negative x it approaches 0.

Now let me check the key structural form: **cubic polynomial in P (with no P term or constant) + P*sigmoid(P)**.

The sigmoid term = α*P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))). This is NOT a simple exponential, log, sin, or polynomial.

Let me think about what forms could match:

The term P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))) can be related to log(1+exp(...)):
- d/dP [log(1+exp(a*(P-d)))] = a*exp(a*(P-d))/(1+exp(a*(P-d))) = a/(1+exp(-a*(P-d)))

So P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))) is NOT simply log(1+exp(...)), but they're related.

Actually, let me try integration by parts or direct algebraic manipulation:

P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))) = P * sigmoid(a*(P-d))

This is P times a sigmoid, which is distinct from log(1+exp(...)).

However, we can write:
P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))) = P - P/(1+exp(a*(P-d)))

Hmm, that doesn't simplify things.

Let me check: can P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))) be expressed using exp(P*c)?

For the sigmoid: 1/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))) = exp(a*(P-d))/(1+exp(a*(P-d)))

So P*exp(a*(P-d))/(1+exp(a*(P-d)))

This is NOT equivalent to c*exp(P*c) or c*log(c*exp(P*c)+1) in general.

Let me verify: log(c₅*exp(P*c₆) + 1). The derivative w.r.t. P is c₆*c₅*exp(P*c₆)/(c₅*exp(P*c₆)+1). This is a sigmoid-like function, not P*sigmoid.

So the GT has the form: **cubic in P + P·sigmoid(P)**.

Now, which candidates could match?

Candidates with P/(something with exp): The GT has P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))), which is P·sigmoid.

Let me look for candidates that have both polynomial terms (up to cubic) AND a P·sigmoid or equivalent term.

Looking through candidates:

**Candidate 62**: (P*(P²c₀ + Pc₁ + c₂) + c₃*(P + c₄)*log(c₅*exp(P*c₆) + 1))/(P + c₄)

The first part is a rational function (cubic/linear), not a polynomial. Unless c₄ = 0, then it becomes P²c₀ + Pc₁ + c₂ + c₃*log(c₅*exp(P*c₆)+1). But GT has P·sigmoid, not log(1+exp).

α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(P-d)))

Can this be rewritten? Let me set u = a*(P-d):
= α*P/(1+exp(-u)) = α*P*exp(u)/(1+exp(u))

= c₀*P/(P+c₁) + c₂*c₃*P² + c₂*P + c₄*exp(P*c₅)

This has P/(P+c₁) which is a rational function, not P·sigmoid. Not matching.

**Candidate 25**: (c₀ + (P*c₁ + c₂)*(P*c₃*(P*c₄ + 1) + c₅*exp(P*c₆)))/(P*c₁ + c₂)

= c₀/(P*c₁+c₂) + P*c₃*(P*c₄+1) + c₅*exp(P*c₆)

Not matching (has 1/(linear) + polynomial + exp, not P·sigmoid).

Now, let me reconsider. The GT sigmoid term is:
α*P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d)))

For the specific parameter values, a ≈ 8 and d ≈ 0.59. The sigmoid transition happens around P ≈ 0.59. For P >> 0.59, the sigmoid ≈ 1, so the term ≈ α*P. For P << 0.59 (but P ≥ 0), the sigmoid ≈ 0.

But we need EXACT equivalence, not approximations.

Let me reconsider whether any candidate can produce P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))).

Note: P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))) = P - P*exp(-a*(P-d))/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))) = P - P/(1+exp(a*(P-d)))

Alternatively: P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))) = P*exp(a*P)*exp(-a*d)/(1+exp(a*P)*exp(-a*d))

If we let β = exp(-a*d), then = P*β*exp(aP)/(1+β*exp(aP))

Now, d/dP[log(1+β*exp(aP))] = a*β*exp(aP)/(1+β*exp(aP))

So β*exp(aP)/(1+β*exp(aP)) = (1/a)*d/dP[log(1+β*exp(aP))]

But we need P times this, which is not simply log(1+β*exp(aP)).

Integration by parts: ∫ P * f'(P) dP = P*f(P) - ∫f(P)dP, but we're not integrating, we need exact functional form.

So P·sigmoid(aP+b) is a fundamentally different basis function from log(1+c·exp(aP)), exp(aP), sin, polynomials, etc.

The only way to get P/(1+exp(...)) is to have it explicitly in the formula structure, like P/(c + exp(...)) or through a ratio that creates it.

Let me look for candidates with P/(... + exp(...)):

Looking at the GT structure: the third term is c₈*P/(c₉ + exp(-c₁₀*(-c₁₁ + P)))

This is literally P divided by (constant + exp(...)). 

None of the candidates seem to have this exact structure. Let me look more carefully...

Actually, wait. Let me re-examine candidates with rational structures involving exp.

**Candidate 97**: (P²(Pc₀+c₁) + c₂(P+c₃)exp(Pc₄))/(P+c₃)
= P²(Pc₀+c₁)/(P+c₃) + c₂*exp(Pc₄)

If I set c₃ = 0: P(Pc₀+c₁) + c₂*exp(Pc₄) = c₀P² + c₁P + c₂*exp(Pc₄). This is quadratic + exp, missing the P·sigmoid and cubic terms.

**Candidate 73**: (P(P²c₀+Pc₁+c₂) + c₃(P+c₄)exp(Pc₅))/(P+c₄)
= P(P²c₀+Pc₁+c₂)/(P+c₄) + c₃*exp(Pc₅)

If c₄=0: P²c₀+Pc₁+c₂ + c₃*exp(Pc₅). Missing cubic and sigmoid.

Hmm, none of these produce P·sigmoid.

Let me reconsider. Maybe I should look at this differently. The GT has three terms. Let me expand the polynomial part fully:

GT = -(α/(ab))P³ + (α/a)P² + αP/(1+exp(-a(P-d)))

With numerical values:
- α/(ab) = 0.1387/(8.038*70.018) ≈ 0.1387/562.8 ≈ 0.000246
- α/a = 0.1387/8.038 ≈ 0.01726

So GT ≈ -0.000246P³ + 0.01726P² + 0.1387P/(1+exp(-8.038(P-0.5894)))

The key question: which candidates have the structural form of cubic polynomial + P·sigmoid?

Actually, I realize I should check if P/(1+exp(-a(P-d))) can be decomposed differently.

P/(1+exp(-a(P-d))) = P·σ(a(P-d)) where σ is the logistic sigmoid.

This cannot be written as a polynomial, exponential, log(1+exp), sin, or any combination thereof (exactly). It's a distinct function.

So I need candidates that either:
1. Explicitly contain P/(c+exp(f(P))) structure, or
2. Can algebraically produce it through ratios

Let me search more carefully through all candidates for structures that could yield P/(1+exp(...)):

None of the candidates have a bare P/(c+exp(...)) term.

Could any rational structure produce it? For example, if we have (... + c·P·exp(aP))/(... + exp(aP)), we could get P·exp(aP)/(1+c·exp(aP)) type terms.

Let me look at candidates with exp in numerator and denominator... None of the candidates have exp in the denominator explicitly.

Wait, I need to reconsider. Let me look at the GT again more carefully:

GT = α(-1+P/a)(1-P/b)P + α(1-P/b)P + αP/(1+exp(-a(-d+P)))

The third term αP/(1+exp(-a(P-d))). 

Hmm, but what about log(1+exp(...))? Let's see:

d/dP [log(1+c·exp(aP))] = a·c·exp(aP)/(1+c·exp(aP))

This is NOT P/(1+exp(...)), it's a sigmoid without the P factor.

What about P·log(1+exp(...))? This is also different.

So the GT contains a fundamentally unique term P·sigmoid that most candidates cannot reproduce.

Let me now check each candidate systematically, focusing on whether they can produce the required basis functions.

The GT requires: {P³, P², P·sigmoid(P)} as basis functions (where sigmoid involves exp).

Actually, wait. Let me reconsider whether the GT could be rewritten differently. 

GT = -(α/(ab))P³ + (α/a)P² + αP/(1+exp(-a(P-d)))

The sigmoid term: for P ≥ 0, this is a smooth function. Can it be approximated by... no, we need EXACT match.

Let me reconsider: could P/(1+exp(-a(P-d))) be written as some combination involving log(1+exp(...))?

P/(1+exp(-a(P-d))) = P·exp(a(P-d))/(1+exp(a(P-d)))

Let f(P) = log(1+exp(a(P-d))). Then f'(P) = a·exp(a(P-d))/(1+exp(a(P-d)))

So exp(a(P-d))/(1+exp(a(P-d))) = f'(P)/a

And P·f'(P)/a is what we need. But P·f'(P) ≠ f(P) in general.

Actually, P·f'(P) = P·d/dP[f(P)]. This is not equal to f(P) or any simple transformation of f(P).

So log(1+exp(...)) candidates cannot match.

What about candidates with exp(P·c) terms? 

exp(a·P) is linearly independent from P/(1+exp(a·P+b)). So candidates with just polynomial + exp cannot match either.

What about candidates with sin terms? sin is linearly independent from sigmoid, so no.

What about candidates with P^c (power law) terms? Also linearly independent.

This means most candidates will NOT match. Let me verify this conclusion by checking if there's any clever algebraic trick I'm missing.

Actually, let me reconsider the GT expression once more. The original symbolic form is:

c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*P/(c9 + exp(-c10*(-c11 + P)))

With c0=c5=c8=α, c1=c3=c6=1, c2=c10=a, c4=c7=b, c9=1, c11=d.

So the structure is: polynomial(P) + P/(1+exp(linear in P))

The P/(1+exp(...)) term is the critical distinguishing feature.

Now let me check: is there ANY candidate that has P/(c+exp(f(P))) or an equivalent structure?

Going through all candidates... I see candidates with:
- exp(P*c): many candidates
- log(c*exp(P*c)+1): candidates 5, 7, 47, 62, 70, 82, 83, 84
- sin/cos: many candidates
- P^c: some candidates
- Rational functions: some candidates

None have P/(c+exp(...)) explicitly.

But wait - could a rational function involving exp produce P·sigmoid?

Consider: (numerator with P·exp(aP))/(denominator with 1+exp(aP))

For example, candidate 73: (P(P²c₀+Pc₁+c₂) + c₃(P+c₄)exp(Pc₅))/(P+c₄)

This gives: P(P²c₀+Pc₁+c₂)/(P+c₄) + c₃exp(Pc₅)

No exp in denominator, so no sigmoid.

None of the candidates have exp in the denominator. The denominators are all polynomial in P (or involve t).

So the sigmoid term P/(1+exp(...)) cannot be produced by any candidate.

Wait, but I should double-check: could log(c·exp(aP)+1) somehow be equivalent to P/(1+exp(-aP+b)) for specific constants? 

log(c·exp(aP)+1) vs P/(1+exp(-a(P-d)))

These are fundamentally different functions. log(c·exp(aP)+1) grows linearly for large aP (≈ aP + log(c)) and approaches 0 for large negative aP. Meanwhile P/(1+exp(-a(P-d))) grows linearly (≈P) for large P and approaches 0 for small P. But their functional forms are different - one is a log, the other is P times a sigmoid.

For large P: log(c·exp(aP)+1) ≈ aP + log(c), while P/(1+exp(-a(P-d))) ≈ P. These have different slopes unless a=1, but even then log(c·exp(P)+1) ≈ P+log(c) while P·sigmoid ≈ P. For small P: log(c·exp(aP)+1) ≈ log(c+1) (constant), while P·sigmoid ≈ 0.

So they're different. No candidate with log(1+exp) can match.

Actually, wait. Let me reconsider. The GT has three parts. What if the polynomial parts and the sigmoid part combine in a way that could be decomposed differently?

GT = -(α/(ab))P³ + (α/a)P² + αP/(1+exp(-a(P-d)))

Could this be rewritten as, say, polynomial + c·log(1+exp(...))?

-(α/(ab))P³ + (α/a)P² + αP/(1+exp(-a(P-d))) = polynomial + c·log(1+exp(aP+b)) ?

For this to work: αP/(1+exp(-a(P-d))) - c·log(1+exp(aP+b)) would need to be a polynomial. But P·sigmoid and log(1+exp) are both non-polynomial, and their difference is also non-polynomial (they have different functional forms). So no.

Could it be polynomial + c·exp(aP)?

αP/(1+exp(-a(P-d))) - c·exp(aP) would need to be polynomial. For large P, P·sigmoid ≈ P while c·exp(aP) grows exponentially. So c must be 0, but then P·sigmoid is not polynomial. No.

I'm now fairly confident that NO candidate can match the GT, because none of them contain the P/(c+exp(...)) or P·sigmoid structure.

But let me do one more check. Let me verify that the GT truly requires this sigmoid term and it can't be zero.

c8 = 0.1387... ≠ 0, and c8 is a GT constant (fixed). So the sigmoid term is present and non-zero.

Actually, wait. Let me re-read the problem statement: "GT constants are FIXED" and "Candidate constants are FREE."

So the GT is fixed with its sigmoid term, and no candidate can reproduce it.

Let me still go through each candidate briefly to be thorough:

None of the 97 candidates contain the P/(constant + exp(linear in P)) structure needed to match the GT.

Actually, I want to reconsider candidates with rational structures more carefully.

**Candidate 26**: (P³c₀ + P²c₁ + Pc₂ + c₃(P+c₄)exp(Pc₅) + c₆t + c₇)/(P+c₄)

Setting c₆=0 (eliminate t): (P³c₀ + P²c₁ + Pc₂ + c₃(P+c₄)exp(Pc₅) + c₇)/(P+c₄)

= (P³c₀ + P²c₁ + Pc₂ + c₇)/(P+c₄) + c₃exp(Pc₅)
